Here is a fun fact. Let's take the iconic pair of Levi's jeans. To make that pair of jeans required a fabric mill to make the denim used in a pair of Levi's located somewhere in the US. The zippers and rivets came from another factory in the US. The thread that stitched the pieces of denim used to come from a mill in the US. The factory that cut and sewed all the pieces together used to be all located in the US. These were all American jobs from at the very least 4 different Mills and Factories in the US. Now a pair of Levi's is usually made in either Mexico or some South American country. You can multiply that across the country with all sorts of products that used to made here and it becomes mind boggling.

No mention of the major problem of getting empty containers back to China. THAT is the issue. China stopped taking the west‚Äôs garbage for recycling in 2018 and since there is almost nothing to ship to China, etc, all the empty containers are stuck in the import ports so they‚Äôre not getting cleared, so no space for incoming full containers‚Ä¶.
What nobody wants to talk about is the Jones Act. This an old maritime law that prohibits foreign ships from moving freight between US ports. Which means if a Chinese ship wants to trade with more than one American port, it has to make one stop, go all the way back to China, and cross the Pacific again. No one actually does that so most of the time they'll make one stop at the Port of Los Angeles, which of course clogs that port up with cargo to the determent of the Hawaiian economy. What's worse, it costs three times as much for US ships to move freight than foreign ships, and we pay that cost in some form or another. This is what you get for "protecting" a handful of jobs in an uncompetitive and inefficient industry.  Unfortunately the majority of the voting public is economically illiterate and tends to favour this type of protectionism. They also don't comprehend the relationship between the import tariffs, which Biden refuses to lift, and inflation. Lifting the tariffs won't cure everything, but it'll surely encourage some import competition which will bring prices down.

Cargo Container¬† Bottleneck Idea  Why not:  1) offload all of those empty containers currently sitting on transport chassis¬† to a temporary holding area (miles away),¬† and get those transport chassis¬† back on the road with full containers.   2) Do not require any driver to bring back an¬† empty container in order to pick up a full container (at least until the supply chain gets caught up).   3) Hire some drivers to do nothing more than to remove empty containers from the port,¬† drive them to the temporary holding area (miles away), drop off the empty container, then go back to the port with an empty chassis to puck up another empty container.¬† Repeat this process to free up space at the port to permit full containers to be offloaded to the port, and allow drivers to take them to their destination.   4) If the issue of dropping off empty containers is for the purpose of loading empty containers onto the ships to take back to their point of origin for reuse, then:¬†  a) modify the process to unload at one port (for example LA Port) and do not reload the ship with empty containers at LA Port,¬†  b) instead require the ship to go to Long Beach Port to be reloaded with empty containers.¬†¬†  c) So one port is used for incoming containers, and the other port is for outgoing containers.¬†¬†  d) Empty Containers can be supplied as needed to the Long Beach Port from the temporary holding area (miles away) (hopefully somewhere between LA Port and Long Beach Port).  e) The empty container temporary holding area:  (1) becomes a buffer zone for the excess empty containers,  (2) allows the transport chassis to be freed up to transport full containers,¬†  (3) eliminates the empty containers from being a bottle neck that ties up transport carriers, or ties up LA Port spaces to offload full containers.   5) To keep each Port Financially happy, agree to a fee split based on quantity of containers moved, regardless of if they are full or empty.¬†¬† All parties pulling in the same process direction, instead of each port‚Äôs process completely overwhelmed, because the process has failed to compensate for added demand.  Just an idea for consideration!  A simple solution all parties¬† can implement immediately!  This was my idea after¬† watching 60 minutes segment, I hope it is useful.

Why not:   1) offload all of those empty containers currently sitting on transport chassis  to a temporary holding area (miles away),  and get those transport chassis  back on the road with full containers.   2) Do not require any driver to bring back an  empty container in order to pick up a full container (at least until the supply chain gets caught up).   3) Hire some drivers to do nothing more than to remove empty containers from the port,  drive them to the temporary holding area (miles away), drop off the empty container, then go back to the port with an empty chassis to puck up another empty container.  Repeat this process to free up space at the port to permit full containers to be offloaded to the port, and allow drivers to take them to their destination.   4) If the issue of dropping off empty containers is for the purpose of loading empty containers onto the ships to take back to their point of origin for reuse, then:   a) modify the process to unload at one port (for example LA Port) and do not reload the ship with empty containers at LA Port,   b) instead require the ship to go to Long Beach Port to be reloaded with empty containers.    c) So one port is used for incoming containers, and the other port is for outgoing containers.    d) Empty Containers can be supplied as needed to the Long Beach Port from the temporary holding area (miles away) (hopefully somewhere between LA Port and Long Beach Port).  e) The empty container temporary holding area:  (1) becomes a buffer zone for the excess empty containers,  (2) allows the transport chassis to be freed up to transport full containers,   (3) eliminates the empty containers from being a bottle neck that ties up transport carriers, or ties up LA Port spaces to offload full containers.   5) To keep each Port Financially happy, agree to a fee split based on quantity of containers moved, regardless of if they are full or empty.   All parties pulling in the same process direction, instead of each port‚Äôs process completely overwhelmed, because the process has failed to compensate for added demand.  Just an idea for consideration!  A simple solution all parties  can implement immediately!

The irony of costs for excessive holding of rail cars (demurrage) is that they are intended to incentivize the owner of the cargo to unload and free up the rail car quickly and not to treat a rail car as an extension of their warehouse. In this case the owners of the cargo are prevented access to their goods by the carrier.  Current logistics practice in the US is a shambles..
